19




                                    ADDRESSING S TUDENT NEEDS
                 Focus                                                 Examples of Programs and Services in LCAP Actions
     English Language Arts             •   Strengthen literacy programs that include explicit phonics instruction and intervention (Based on the successful
                                           model at Dyer Kelly for the Early Literacy Support Block grant).
                                       •   English Language Development strategies and Universal Design for Learning in planning lessons.
                                       •   Promote literacy with families.
                                       •   Language Essentials for Teachers of Reading and Spelling (LETRS) training.
     Math                              •   Professional learning opportunities focused on intervention strategies and resources, implementation of new
                                           curriculum, differentiated instructional strategies, equitable grading practices, and network collaboration.
                                       •   Tiered system of support for teachers to implement early intervention and assessment guided instruction.
                                       •   Support based on diagnostic data for students below grade level in math and reading.
                                       •   Extended learning opportunities during summer for priority student groups to accelerate growth towards math
                                           standards.
     English Learner Progress and      •   Translators to provide information and communicate to students and families in home language.
     Attendance                        •   Instructional technology supports and resources for ELs and students receiving special education services to
                                           ensure inclusion and access to the same academic content.
                                       •   Engage and provide information regarding ELD to students, families, and staff (i.e. process, purpose, pathway,
                                           options, meaning).




                                                                                                                                                              20




20


                                                                                                                                                                   78
                                                                                                                                                                     10
                                                                                                                                                           2/3/2025




                                  ADDRESSING S TUDENT NEEDS
                 Focus                                          Examples of Programs and Services in LCAP Actions
     Behavior and Mental Health    •   Screener to identify students who are at-risk in the areas of academics, behavior, and emotional well being.
                                   •   Greater access to individualized supports for students who are struggling with regulation and behavior.
                                   •   Individualized skill support to students and teach appropriate behavioral strategies.
                                   •   Services that assist students and families in navigating the mental health system to get access to care.

     College and Career            •   College and career readiness counseling to provide tailored guidance on post-secondary options, financial aid,
                                       and language support.
                                   •   Culturally responsive mentorship and school counseling to provide socio-emotional support that addresses
                                       barriers to academic success and fosters holistic development.
                                   •   College preparation assistance, outreach, support and resource information, student/parent consultation and
                                       workshops, course selection and career development assistance, and access to financial aid and scholarships.

     Class Size Reduction          •   Class size reduction pilot with six highest-density schools in secondary and K-8: Encina High, San Juan High,
                                       Arcade Middle, Katherine Johnson Middle, Starr King K-8, and Kingswood K-8.
                                   •   Reduce class sizes and practitioner-to-student ratios.
                                   •   Improve working conditions for staff and learning conditions for students.
                                   •   Stabilize staffing at highest-need schools to maintain continuity of learning.
                                   •   Increase opportunities for differentiated instruction.

SUBJECT: Choices Charter School 2024-2025 Local Control and Accountability Plan (LCAP) Mid-Year
Update (Oaxaca) - 7:55 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Report: The superintendent is recommending that the board review the Choices Charter School 2024-2025 LCAP
mid-year update.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The 2024-2027 LCAP is a three-year plan that supports the continuous improvement of student performance within
the eight state priorities, with an emphasis on English learner, low income, and foster youth students. The LCAP is
updated yearly based on a review of state and local data, input gathered from consulting with our educational
partners, and research. The governing board adopted the Choices Charter School 2024-2025 LCAP on June 25,
2024. The LCAP mid-year update includes available mid-year data and expenditures related to metrics and actions
in the 2024-2025 LCAP.
ATTACHMENT(S):

February 2025



                           Attachment 2:
                           Successes &
                Primary Challenges / Areas of Growth
Successes
1) Choices educates all students in an equitable manner.

   A. 2024 CAASPP and ELPAC scores of CCS’s All Students and Student Subgroups demonstrate
      that Choices’ educational program is both effective and equitable:
      https://caaspp-elpac.ets.org/caaspp/, https://www.caschooldashboard.org/
              ➢ CCS All Students (AS):
                 ✓ Demonstrated growth in Math
              ➢ CCS Socioeconomically Disadvantaged Students (SDS):
                 ✓ Outperformed the State of California SDS in Science
                 ✓ Performed as well as CCS AS in Science
              ➢ CCS Students with Disabilities (SWD):
                 ✓ Demonstrated growth in English Language Arts
                 ✓ Outperformed the State of California SWD in English Language Arts & Science
              ➢ CCS English Learners (Ever-EL Students) (EL):
                 ✓ Demonstrated growth in Math
                 ✓ Outperformed the State of California EL in Science
                 ✓ Performed as well as CCS AS in Science
              ➢ CCS English Learners (EL):
                 ✓ Demonstrated growth in the percentage making progress towards EL proficiency

   B. 2024 Graduation Rates also demonstrate the equitable nature of the CCS program. CCS's
      Student Subgroups graduate at rates about the same or greater than CCS's AS.
      https://dq.cde.ca.gov/dataquest/
              ➢ CCS AS: 71%
              ➢ CCS SDS: 70%
              ➢ CCS SWD: 80%

   C. 2024 Student Satisfaction Survey results confirm the equitability of the program:
            ➢ 100% of students report that the program serves all students in an equitable (fair,
               unbiased, non-discriminatory) fashion.
            ➢ 97% of students feel accepted and included.

2) Choices students typically enroll with deficiencies in skills and credits but grow
   academically while at CCS and graduate within five years.

   A. 2023-24 iReady data demonstrates academic growth experienced by Choices students after
      just one semester of continuous enrollment. https://login.i-ready.com/
             ➢ A greater percentage of students perform at or above grade level:
                ✓ Math: 19% in Fall vs. 26% in Winter
                ✓ Reading: 37% in Fall vs. 38% in Winter
             ➢ Fewer students perform at two or more years behind grade level:
                ✓ Math: 64% in Fall vs. 55% in Winter
                ✓ Reading: 41% in Fall vs. 40% in Winter
                                                                                                    139
                                                                                                    1
February 2025


3) Choices students are engaged in their education.

   A. 2023-24 Chronic Absenteeism (CA) data demonstrates that Choices students are
      experiencing declining rates of disengagement each year and are closely aligned with students
      throughout the state with respect to this metric. https://www.caschooldashboard.org/
            ➢ CCS CA = 20%, State of California CA = 19%

   B. 2023-24 Expulsion Rate data demonstrates that Choices students are rarely expelled.
      https://dq.cde.ca.gov/dataquest/
              ➢ CCS Expulsion Rate has been 0% for more than a decade.

   C. 2023-24 Suspension Rate data demonstrates that Choices students are rarely suspended.
      https://www.caschooldashboard.org/
              ➢ CCS Suspension Rate has been 0%/Blue for each year that a rating has been
                available on the California School Dashboard since its inception in 2017.

4) Choices students feel safe and cared for, and roughly half report less anxiety since they
   enrolled.

   A. Data from the 2024 Students School Satisfaction Survey and the 2024 Students with
      Disabilities Attitude Survey demonstrates that students feel safe, cared for, and less anxious
      while they learn.
             ➢ 97% of All Students and 94% of Students with Disabilities report that they feel safe
                 on campus.
             ➢ 100% of All Students feel that the Choices staff is caring and responsive to student
                 needs.
             ➢ 62% of All Students and 48% of Students with Disabilities report that they have
                 experienced less anxiety since enrolling at Choices.

Primary Challenges / Areas of Growth:
1) College Career Indicator (College & Career Readiness)

      A. Because Choices students often face more obstacles to their academic success than the
         average student, most prefer to pursue a more gradual approach to college and career,
         choosing to continue to community college, vocational school, or the work force after
         graduation. These options do not require students to participate in most of the activities
         that would qualify them as “Prepared” on the Dashboard. Though this reality limits CCS’s
         ability to match state CCI averages, CCS recognizes that some growth in this area is
         needed.

2) Math CAASPP Scores (Math Proficiency)

      B. Math proficiency is consistently a challenge at Choices. Students typically enroll with
         significant gaps in skills and make progress once enrolled. Recent i-Ready data shows
         that students build skills quickly once at Choices, but this growth is not readily detected on
         CAASPP exams. CAASPP scores are only a partially accurate reflection of the
         effectiveness of the education that Choices provides, but CCS will continue to explore ways
         to improve long term Math growth and achievement.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                      AGENDA ITEM:                     H.4
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                      MEETING DATE:                 02/11/2025

SUBJECT: Revisions to Board Policy 6145.6 International Exchange (Oaxaca) - 8:05 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Discussion: The superintendent is recommending that the board discuss the proposed revisions to Board Policy
6145.6 International Exchange. Action anticipated: 02/25/2025.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
San Juan Unified has long recognized that contact between students of different countries and cultures promotes
global awareness and international understanding.

On average, San Juan Unified has between five and ten international exchange students a year who attend high
schools throughout the district. Current policy only allows for exchange students to participate in full year
programs. There is community interest to allow an option to participate in either a semester or full year. High
school principals and secondary district teams are in support of this action.

In reviewing policies around the area and state, most school districts allow placements for part of the school year
and do not mandate a full year.

The revised policy reflects the recommendation to allow the option for either one semester or full year participation
for an international exchange program.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Board Policy 6145.6 International Exchange Policy

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 02/03/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                 Brian Ginter, Director, Admissions and Family Services

APPROVED BY:                 F.J. "Harvey" Oaxaca, Ed.D., Assistant Superintendent, Educational Services
                             Amy L. Slavensky, Ph.D., Interim Deputy Superintendent, Schools & Student Support
                             Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                                        148
                                                                              Board Policy Manual
                                                                    San Juan Unified School District

Policy 6145.6: International Exchange                                             Status: ADOPTED

Original Adopted Date: 02/12/2008 | Last Revised Date: 04/26/2011



The Governing Board recognizes that personal contact between students of different countries and
cultures promotes global awareness and international understanding. To that end, the Board
welcomes the enrollment of international exchange high school students and further encourages
District students to take advantage of opportunities that they may have to participate in such
programs which allow them to study in another country.
International Exchange Student Programs
To enroll in a District high school, an international exchange student must be participating in an
exchange program registered with the California Attorney General's Office, designated by the U.S.
Department of State and accepted for listing on the Council for Standards for International
Educational Travel's Advisory List ("CSIET"). Enrollment of international exchange students will be
handled through the office of the Director of Admissions and Family Services.
To ensure that District facilities will not be overcrowded, or, when necessary because of limited
District resources, the Superintendent or designee may limit the number of international exchange
students to be accepted at any District high school. The Superintendent or designee shall establish
District criteria for accepting international exchange students into the District. Enrollment for
international exchange students shall be for one year only. The District will not may accept
applications for single semester placements or full year placements.
The District shall not incur any financial obligations when sending and/or receiving international
exchange students. Program sponsors shall provide assurance of their responsibility for health/
accident/liability insurance, the student's home placement, and the resolution of any related
personal difficulties which may arise.
District criteria for issuing regular diplomas to international exchange students shall be consistent
with state graduation requirements. The principal or designee shall refer to the state graduation
requirements when assisting international exchange students in selecting classes and cocurricular
activities based on the student's individual qualifications, needs, and interests.
District credit for courses successfully completed in the foreign country shall be granted in
accordance with Board policy and administrative regulation. District students seeking District
graduation credit for courses successfully completed in the foreign country must provide evidence
of academic progress.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                     AGENDA ITEM:                    H.5
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                     MEETING DATE:                02/11/2025

SUBJECT: Public Hearing: Resolution Authorizing and Approving Cottage Elementary School Project #108-
9568-P2 (Camarda) - 8:10 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
Public Hearing/Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board hold a public hearing to solicit public
comment regarding the Cottage Elementary School portable project #108-9568-P2 being proposed for submission
for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b). After the public hearing is conducted, the superintendent is
recommending that the board adopt Resolution No. 4187, authorizing and approving Project #108-9568-P2.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The Kindergarten Through Grade 12 Schools and Local Community College Public Education Facilities
Modernization, Repair, and Safety Bond Act of 2024 ("Act"), Education Code sections 101400 et seq., provides
statewide funding for new construction and modernization of school facilities for specified purposes. Education
Code section 101460(b) requires that, before approving a project or project(s) seeking funds under the Act, the
governing board of a school district must hold at least one public hearing to solicit input from members of the
public regarding the project or project(s) being proposed for submission for funding.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Resolution No. 4187

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 02/03/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                Frank Camarda, Chief Operations Officer

APPROVED BY:                Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                                     150
                                              Attachment 1


    RESOLUTION BEFORE THE BOARD OF EDUCATION OF THE SAN JUAN UNIFIED
      SCHOOL DISTRICT TO AUTHORIZE AND APPROVE PROJECT #108-9568-P2
     FOLLOWING PUBLIC HEARING UNDER EDUCATION CODE SECTION 101460.

                                        RESOLUTION NO. 4187

          WHEREAS, the Kindergarten Through Grade 12 Schools and Local Community College Public
Education Facilities Modernization, Repair, and Safety Bond Act of 2024 (“Act”), Education Code
sections 101400 et seq., provides statewide funding for new construction and modernization of school
facilities for specified purposes;

        WHEREAS, Education Code section 101460(b) requires that, before approving a project or
project(s) seeking funds under the Act, the governing board of a school district must hold at least one
public hearing to solicit input from members of the public regarding the project or project(s) being
proposed for submission for funding;

       WHEREAS, the San Juan Unified School District (“District”) provided public notice of the
hearing regarding the project(s) identified below in its meeting agenda posted to its website on
02/07/2025 as well as in a separate notice posted to the website on 02/03/2025

        WHEREAS, at its regularly-scheduled and publicly-noticed meeting occurring on 02/11/2025,
the District’s Board of Education (“Board”) has conducted the hearing required by section 101460(b) to
consider the following project(s) (“Project”):

Project                  Location               General Description           Estimated     Estimated
                                                                              Cost          Timeframe

Cottage Portable         2221 Morse Ave,        Two classrooms,               $1,445,000    June 2025 –

                         CA 95825               utilities, wood foundation,
                                                path of travel, low voltage
                                                and electrical hook-ups
                                                associated with the
                                                installation of District
                                                owned portable
                                                classrooms.


       WHEREAS, the modernization Project(s) are the type permitted by Education Code section
101412(b);

        WHEREAS, public input provided at the hearing does not alter the District’s intent to enter into
the Project(s), but will be taken into account in implementing the Project(s);

        WHEREAS, for other project(s), the District has contracted for the independent performance of
audits in accordance with Education Code section 41024 and, if the Project(s) above are approved,
intends to contract for such audits of the Project(s), as required by Education Code section 101460(a), to
ensure that the use of the funds has been reviewed for expenditure consistent with the requirements of all
applicable laws;

          WHEREAS, the District desires to implement the Project(s) identified above.




                                                    1                                                        151
        NOW, THEREFORE, the District’s Board of Education does hereby determine, resolve, and
order as follows:



        Section 1.      That the recitals set forth above are true and correct.

        Section 2.       That, following the public hearing occurring prior to adoption of this Resolution,
the Board approves proceeding with each of the Project(s) considered, which are understood to be
consistent with the scope of the Act.

        Section 3.       That District staff is directed to consider public comments received at the public
hearing in further defining and implementing each of the Project(s).

        Section 4.      That District staff is directed to proceed with applying for funding for each of the
Project(s) in accordance with requirements of the Act and any regulations or other guidance that may be
adopted thereunder.

         Section 5.      That information regarding each of the Project(s), including without limitation its
description, location, estimated costs, and estimated timeline for completion, shall be posted to the
District website.

        Section 6.       That District staff shall retain all financial accounts, documents, and records
necessary for the independent performance audit of each of the Project(s) required by Education Code
section 101460(a); shall provide for audits of each Project in accordance with Education Code section
41024; and shall post the results of such audits to the District website.



        PASSED AND ADOPTED this 11th day of February 2025, by the following vote of the Board:

        AYES:
        NOES:

Modernization, Repair, and Safety Bond Act of 2024 ("Act"), Education Code sections 101400 et seq., provides
statewide funding for new construction and modernization of school facilities for specified purposes. Education
Code section 101460(b) requires that, before approving a project or project(s) seeking funds under the Act, the
governing board of a school district must hold at least one public hearing to solicit input from members of the
public regarding the project or project(s) being proposed for submission for funding.

Starr King K-8          4848 Cottage Way,      Two classrooms,               $1,245,000     June 2025 –
Portable                Carmichael, CA         Sitework, underground                        August 2025
                        95608                  utilities, wood foundation,
                                               path of travel, low voltage
                                               and electrical hook-ups
                                               associated with the
                                               relocation of and
                                               installation of District
                                               owned portable
                                               classrooms.


       WHEREAS, the modernization Project(s) are the type permitted by Education Code section
101412(b);

        WHEREAS, public input provided at the hearing does not alter the District’s intent to enter into
the Project(s), but will be taken into account in implementing the Project(s);

        WHEREAS, for other project(s), the District has contracted for the independent performance of
audits in accordance with Education Code section 41024 and, if the Project(s) above are approved,
intends to contract for such audits of the Project(s), as required by Education Code section 101460(a), to
ensure that the use of the funds has been reviewed for expenditure consistent with the requirements of all
applicable laws;




                                                    1                                                        166
        WHEREAS, the District desires to implement the Project(s) identified above.

        NOW, THEREFORE, the District’s Board of Education does hereby determine, resolve, and
order as follows:



        Section 1.      That the recitals set forth above are true and correct.

        Section 2.       That, following the public hearing occurring prior to adoption of this Resolution,
the Board approves proceeding with each of the Project(s) considered, which are understood to be
consistent with the scope of the Act.

        Section 3.       That District staff is directed to consider public comments received at the public
hearing in further defining and implementing each of the Project(s).

        Section 4.      That District staff is directed to proceed with applying for funding for each of the
Project(s) in accordance with requirements of the Act and any regulations or other guidance that may be
adopted thereunder.

         Section 5.      That information regarding each of the Project(s), including without limitation its
description, location, estimated costs, and estimated timeline for completion, shall be posted to the
District website.

        Section 6.       That District staff shall retain all financial accounts, documents, and records
necessary for the independent performance audit of each of the Project(s) required by Education Code
section 101460(a); shall provide for audits of each Project in accordance with Education Code section
41024; and shall post the results of such audits to the District website.



        PASSED AND ADOPTED this 11th day of February 2025, by the following vote of the Board:

        AYES:
        NOES:
        ABSENT:
        ABSTAIN:

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                   AGENDA ITEM:                    H.11
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                   MEETING DATE:                02/11/2025

SUBJECT: Public Hearing: Resolution Authorizing and Approving Whitney Avenue Elementary School
Project #152-9568-P1 (Camarda) - 8:40 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
Public Hearing/Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board hold a public hearing to solicit public
comment regarding the Whitney Avenue Elementary School portable project #152-9568-P1 being proposed for
submission for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b). After the public hearing is conducted, the
superintendent is recommending that the board adopt Resolution No. 4193, authorizing and approving Project
#152-9568-P1.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The Kindergarten Through Grade 12 Schools and Local Community College Public Education Facilities
Modernization, Repair, and Safety Bond Act of 2024 ("Act"), Education Code sections 101400 et seq., provides
statewide funding for new construction and modernization of school facilities for specified purposes. Education
Code section 101460(b) requires that, before approving a project or project(s) seeking funds under the Act, the
governing board of a school district must hold at least one public hearing to solicit input from members of the
public regarding the project or project(s) being proposed for submission for funding.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Resolution No. 4193

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A
PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 02/03/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                Frank Camarda, Chief Operations Officer

APPROVED BY:                Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools

    RESOLUTION BEFORE THE BOARD OF EDUCATION OF THE SAN JUAN UNIFIED
      SCHOOL DISTRICT TO AUTHORIZE AND APPROVE PROJECT #152-9568-P1
     FOLLOWING PUBLIC HEARING UNDER EDUCATION CODE SECTION 101460.

                                       RESOLUTION NO. 4193

          WHEREAS, the Kindergarten Through Grade 12 Schools and Local Community College Public
Education Facilities Modernization, Repair, and Safety Bond Act of 2024 (“Act”), Education Code
sections 101400 et seq., provides statewide funding for new construction and modernization of school
facilities for specified purposes;

        WHEREAS, Education Code section 101460(b) requires that, before approving a project or
project(s) seeking funds under the Act, the governing board of a school district must hold at least one
public hearing to solicit input from members of the public regarding the project or project(s) being
proposed for submission for funding;

       WHEREAS, the San Juan Unified School District (“District”) provided public notice of the
hearing regarding the project(s) identified below in its meeting agenda posted to its website on
02/07/2025 as well as in a separate notice posted to the website on 02/03/2025

        WHEREAS, at its regularly-scheduled and publicly-noticed meeting occurring on 02/11/2025,
the District’s Board of Education (“Board”) has conducted the hearing required by section 101460(b) to
consider the following project(s) (“Project”):

Project                 Location               General Description           Estimated      Estimated
                                                                             Cost           Timeframe

Whitney Avenue          4248 Whitney Ave,      Two classrooms,               $1,235,000     June 2025 –
Elementary Portable     Sacramento, CA         Sitework, underground                        August 2025
                        95821                  utilities, wood foundation,
                                               path of travel, low voltage
                                               and electrical hook-ups
                                               associated with the
                                               relocation of and
                                               installation of District
                                               owned portable
                                               classrooms.


       WHEREAS, the modernization Project(s) are the type permitted by Education Code section
101412(b);

        WHEREAS, public input provided at the hearing does not alter the District’s intent to enter into
the Project(s), but will be taken into account in implementing the Project(s);

        WHEREAS, for other project(s), the District has contracted for the independent performance of
audits in accordance with Education Code section 41024 and, if the Project(s) above are approved,
intends to contract for such audits of the Project(s), as required by Education Code section 101460(a), to
ensure that the use of the funds has been reviewed for expenditure consistent with the requirements of all
applicable laws;




                                                    1                                                        169
        WHEREAS, the District desires to implement the Project(s) identified above.

        NOW, THEREFORE, the District’s Board of Education does hereby determine, resolve, and
order as follows:



        Section 1.      That the recitals set forth above are true and correct.

        Section 2.       That, following the public hearing occurring prior to adoption of this Resolution,
the Board approves proceeding with each of the Project(s) considered, which are understood to be
consistent with the scope of the Act.

        Section 3.       That District staff is directed to consider public comments received at the public
hearing in further defining and implementing each of the Project(s).

        Section 4.      That District staff is directed to proceed with applying for funding for each of the
Project(s) in accordance with requirements of the Act and any regulations or other guidance that may be
adopted thereunder.

         Section 5.      That information regarding each of the Project(s), including without limitation its
description, location, estimated costs, and estimated timeline for completion, shall be posted to the
District website.

        Section 6.       That District staff shall retain all financial accounts, documents, and records
necessary for the independent performance audit of each of the Project(s) required by Education Code
section 101460(a); shall provide for audits of each Project in accordance with Education Code section
41024; and shall post the results of such audits to the District website.



        PASSED AND ADOPTED this 11th day of February 2025, by the following vote of the Board:

        AYES:
        NOES:
        ABSENT:
        ABSTAIN:
